Some cities, such as Dayton, owe their industrial emergence to their location on canals, and as late as 1910 interior canals carried much of the bulk freight of the state.
</p><p>Areas under the protection of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> include <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Valley_National_Park" title="Cuyahoga Valley National Park">Cuyahoga Valley National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hopewell_Culture_National_Historical_Park" title="Hopewell Culture National Historical Park">Hopewell Culture National Historical Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Aviation_Heritage_National_Historical_Park" title="Dayton Aviation Heritage National Historical Park">Dayton Aviation Heritage National Historical Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Ladies_National_Historic_Site" title="First Ladies National Historic Site">First Ladies National Historic Site</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield_National_Historic_Site" title="James A. Garfield National Historic Site">James A. Garfield National Historic Site</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft_National_Historic_Site" title="William Howard Taft National Historic Site">William Howard Taft National Historic Site</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Young_Buffalo_Soldiers_National_Monument" title="Charles Young Buffalo Soldiers National Monument">Charles Young Buffalo Soldiers National Monument</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perry%27s_Victory_and_International_Peace_Memorial" title="Perry&#39;s Victory and International Peace Memorial">Perry's Victory and International Peace Memorial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fauna">Fauna</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg/220px-Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg/330px-Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg/440px-Hellbender_Cryptobranchus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Hellbender" title="Hellbender">Eastern Hellbender</a> in captivity</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio has wide variety of unique animal species. Rare and endangered species include the <a href="/wiki/Hellbender" title="Hellbender">Eastern Hellbender</a>, which is found in the Southeastern Appalachian region of Ohio and is classified as state endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The Eastern Hellbender is the 3rd largest <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibian</a> in the world, and can grow up to 27 inches in length. It is fully aquatic and breathes almost entirely through its skin. Due to this, it is only found in pristine, cool, clear, fast flowing streams and rivers. It is highly threatened by <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat loss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Water pollution in the United States">water pollution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sedimentation" title="Sedimentation">sedimentation</a> due to logging and other human activities.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Ohio" title="Climate change in Ohio">Climate change in Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png/220px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="256" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png/330px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png/440px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Ohio.png 2x" data-file-width="1316" data-file-height="1531" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Ohio, using 1991–2020 <a href="/wiki/Climatological_normal" title="Climatological normal">climate normals</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The climate of Ohio is a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa/Dfb</i>) throughout most of the state, except in the extreme southern counties of Ohio's <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_region" title="Bluegrass region">Bluegrass region</a> section, which are located on the northern periphery of the <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<i>Cfa</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Upland_South" title="Upland South">Upland South</a> region of the United States. Summers are typically hot and humid throughout the state, while winters generally range from cool to cold. Precipitation in Ohio is moderate year-round. Severe weather is not uncommon in the state, although there are typically fewer <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> reports in Ohio than in states located in what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>. Severe <a href="/wiki/Lake_effect_snow" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake effect snow">lake effect snowstorms</a> are also not uncommon on the southeast shore of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>, which is located in an area designated as the <a href="/wiki/Snowbelt" title="Snowbelt">Snowbelt</a>.
</p><p>Although predominantly not in a subtropical climate, some warmer-climate flora and fauna do reach well into Ohio. For instance, some trees with more southern ranges, such as the <a href="/wiki/Blackjack_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Blackjack oak">blackjack oak</a>, <i>Quercus marilandica</i>, are found at their northernmost in Ohio just north of the Ohio River. Also evidencing this climatic transition from a subtropical to a continental climate, several plants such as the Southern magnolia <i>(<a href="/wiki/Magnolia_grandiflora" title="Magnolia grandiflora">Magnolia grandiflora</a>)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Albizia_julibrissin" title="Albizia julibrissin">Albizia julibrissin</a> (mimosa), <a href="/wiki/Crape_Myrtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Crape Myrtle">Crape Myrtle</a>, and even the occasional <a href="/wiki/Needle_Palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Needle Palm">Needle Palm</a> are hardy landscape materials regularly used as street, yard, and garden plantings in the <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_region" title="Bluegrass region">Bluegrass region</a> of Ohio; but these same plants will simply not thrive in much of the rest of the state. This interesting change may be observed while traveling through Ohio on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 75 in Ohio">Interstate 75</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a> to <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo</a>; the observant traveler of this diverse state may even catch a glimpse of Cincinnati's <a href="/wiki/Common_wall_lizard" class="mw-redirect" title="Common wall lizard">common wall lizard</a>, one of the few examples of permanent "subtropical" fauna in Ohio.
</p><p>The worst weather disaster in Ohio history occurred along the Great Miami River in 1913. Known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dayton_Flood" title="Great Dayton Flood">Great Dayton Flood</a>, the entire <a href="/wiki/Great_Miami_River" title="Great Miami River">Miami River</a> watershed flooded, including the downtown business district of <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton</a>. As a result, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Conservancy_District" title="Miami Conservancy District">Miami Conservancy District</a> was created as the first major floodplain engineering project in Ohio and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-MCDAct_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCDAct-118">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The highest recorded temperature was 113&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a> (45&#160;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a>), near <a href="/wiki/Gallipolis,_Ohio" title="Gallipolis, Ohio">Gallipolis</a> on July 21, 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The lowest recorded temperature was −39&#160;°F (−39&#160;°C), at <a href="/wiki/Milligan,_Ohio" title="Milligan, Ohio">Milligan</a> on February 10, 1899,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Blizzard_of_1899" title="Great Blizzard of 1899">Great Blizzard of 1899</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</h4></div>
<p>Although few have registered as noticeable to the average resident, more than 200 earthquakes with a <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Richter magnitude scale">magnitude</a> of 2.0 or higher have occurred in Ohio since 1776.<sup id="cite_ref-in-ohio_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-in-ohio-123">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The Western Ohio Seismic Zone and a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Great_Lakes_Seismic_Zone" title="Southern Great Lakes Seismic Zone">Southern Great Lakes Seismic Zone</a> are located in the state, and numerous <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">faults</a> lie under the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-in-ohio_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-in-ohio-123">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most substantial known earthquake in Ohio history was the <a href="/wiki/Anna,_Ohio" title="Anna, Ohio">Anna</a> (Shelby County) earthquake,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> which occurred on March 9, 1937. It was centered in western Ohio, with a magnitude of 5.4, and was of <a href="/wiki/Mercalli_intensity_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercalli intensity scale">intensity</a> VIII.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other significant earthquakes in Ohio include:<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> one of magnitude 4.8 near <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Ohio" title="Lima, Ohio">Lima</a> on September 19, 1884;<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> one of magnitude 4.2 near <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Ohio" title="Portsmouth, Ohio">Portsmouth</a> on May 17, 1901;<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> and one of 5.0 in <a href="/wiki/LeRoy_Township,_Lake_County,_Ohio" title="LeRoy Township, Lake County, Ohio">LeRoy Township in Lake County</a> on January 31, 1986, which continued to trigger 13 aftershocks of magnitude 0.5 to 2.4 for two months.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Notable Ohio earthquakes in the 21st century include one occurring on December 31, 2011, approximately 4 kilometers (2.5&#160;mi) northwest of <a href="/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio" title="Youngstown, Ohio">Youngstown</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and one occurring on June 10, 2019, approximately 5 kilometers (3.1&#160;mi) north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Eastlake,_Ohio" title="Eastlake, Ohio">Eastlake</a> under <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> both registered a 4.0 magnitude.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cities">Cities</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Ohio">List of cities in Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_population_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ohio_population_map.png/220px-Ohio_population_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ohio_population_map.png/330px-Ohio_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ohio_population_map.png/440px-Ohio_population_map.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Ohio population density map</figcaption></figure>
<p>There are 13 <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical areas</a> in Ohio, anchored by 16 cities, as defined by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">Office of Management and Budget</a>. Additionally, 30 Ohio cities function as centers of <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">micropolitan statistical areas</a>, urban clusters smaller than that of metropolitan areas. Ohio's three largest cities are <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>.
</p><p>Columbus is the capital of the state, near its geographic center, and is well known for <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a>. In 2019, the city had six corporations named to the U.S. Fortune 500 list: <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Data" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance Data">Alliance Data</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationwide_Mutual_Insurance_Company" title="Nationwide Mutual Insurance Company">Nationwide Mutual Insurance Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Electric_Power" title="American Electric Power">American Electric Power</a>, <a href="/wiki/L_Brands" class="mw-redirect" title="L Brands">L Brands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Bancshares" title="Huntington Bancshares">Huntington Bancshares</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Health" title="Cardinal Health">Cardinal Health</a> in suburban <a href="/wiki/Dublin,_Ohio" title="Dublin, Ohio">Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GDP_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP-134">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Other major employers include hospitals (among others, <a href="/wiki/Wexner_Medical_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Wexner Medical Center">Wexner Medical Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationwide_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Nationwide Children&#39;s Hospital">Nationwide Children's Hospital</a>), high tech research and development including the <a href="/wiki/Battelle_Memorial_Institute" title="Battelle Memorial Institute">Battelle Memorial Institute</a>, information-based companies such as <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Abstracts_Service" title="Chemical Abstracts Service">Chemical Abstracts Service</a>, manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Worthington_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Worthington Industries">Worthington Industries</a>, and financial institutions such as <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Bancshares" title="Huntington Bancshares">Huntington Bancshares</a>. Fast food chains <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy&#39;s">Wendy's</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Castle_(restaurant)" title="White Castle (restaurant)">White Castle</a> are also headquartered in Columbus.
</p><p>Located in <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio" title="Northeast Ohio">Northeast Ohio</a> along the Lake Erie shore, Cleveland is characterized by its <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> heritage, ethnic immigrant cultures, and history as a major American manufacturing and healthcare center. It anchors the Cleveland–Akron–Canton Combined Statistical Area, of which the industrial cities of <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">Akron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">Canton</a> are constituent parts. <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Ohio" title="Mansfield, Ohio">Mansfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandusky,_Ohio" title="Sandusky, Ohio">Sandusky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio" title="Youngstown, Ohio">Youngstown</a> are also major cities in the region. Northeast Ohio is known for major industrial companies <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Goodyear Tire and Rubber Company">Goodyear Tire and Rubber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timken_Company" title="Timken Company">Timken</a>, top-ranked colleges <a href="/wiki/Case_Western_Reserve_University" title="Case Western Reserve University">Case Western Reserve University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_University" title="Kent State University">Kent State University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Clinic" title="Cleveland Clinic">Cleveland Clinic</a>, and cultural attractions including the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art" title="Cleveland Museum of Art">Cleveland Museum of Art</a>, Big Five member <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Orchestra" title="Cleveland Orchestra">Cleveland Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Valley_National_Park" title="Cuyahoga Valley National Park">Cuyahoga Valley National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playhouse_Square" title="Playhouse Square">Playhouse Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">Cincinnati</a> anchors Southwest Ohio and the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_metropolitan_area" title="Cincinnati metropolitan area">Cincinnati metropolitan area</a>, which also encompasses counties in Kentucky and Indiana. The metropolitan area is home to <a href="/wiki/Miami_University" title="Miami University">Miami University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cincinnati" title="University of Cincinnati">University of Cincinnati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Union_Terminal" title="Cincinnati Union Terminal">Cincinnati Union Terminal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Cincinnati Symphony Orchestra">Cincinnati Symphony Orchestra</a>, and various Fortune 500 companies, including <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s,_Inc." title="Macy&#39;s, Inc.">Macy's, Inc.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Third_Bank" title="Fifth Third Bank">Fifth Third Bank</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Ohio" title="Springfield, Ohio">Springfield</a> are in the Miami Valley, which is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dayton" title="University of Dayton">University of Dayton</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Ballet" title="Dayton Ballet">Dayton Ballet</a>, and the extensive <a href="/wiki/Wright-Patterson_Air_Force_Base" title="Wright-Patterson Air Force Base">Wright-Patterson Air Force Base</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Ohio" title="Lima, Ohio">Lima</a> are the major cities in Northwest Ohio, an area known for its glass-making industry. It is home to <a href="/wiki/Owens_Corning" title="Owens Corning">Owens Corning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Owens-Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Owens-Illinois">Owens-Illinois</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> corporations.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Steubenville,_Ohio" title="Steubenville, Ohio">Steubenville</a> is the only metropolitan city in <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Ohio" title="Appalachian Ohio">Appalachian Ohio</a>, a region known for its <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_mixed_mesophytic_forests" title="Appalachian mixed mesophytic forests">mixed mesophytic forests</a>. Other metropolitan areas that contain cities in Ohio but are primarily in other states include the <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">Huntington, West Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia" title="Wheeling, West Virginia">Wheeling, West Virginia</a> areas. Ohio is the US state with the highest number of cities with the same name as UK cities.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid #a2a9b1;background-color:var(--background-color-neutral-subtle,#f8f9fa);padding:0.3em;font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop caption{background-color:lavender;color:black;padding-right:0.2em;padding-left:0.2em;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold;border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-bottom:none}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop th[scope=col]{border-bottom:1px solid black}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(2){text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;padding-right:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td.us-census-pop-estimate{padding-left:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(3){padding-left:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(4){padding-left:0.5em;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-footnote{border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:center}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-right{float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-left{float:left;clear:left;margin:0 1em 1em 0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-none{float:none;margin:0 1em 1em 0}}</style>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Population">Population</h3></div>
<p>From just over 45,000 residents in 1800, Ohio's population grew faster than 10% per decade (except for the <a href="/wiki/1940_census" class="mw-redirect" title="1940 census">1940 census</a>) until the <a href="/wiki/1970_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="1970 United States Census">1970 census</a>, which recorded just over 10.65 million Ohioans.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Growth then slowed for the next four decades.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> counted 11,808,848 in the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020 census</a>, a 2.4% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2020census_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020census-141">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Ohio's population growth lags that of the entire United States, and <a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">whites</a> are found in a greater density than the U.S. average. As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Ohio's <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Morrow_County,_Ohio" title="Morrow County, Ohio">Morrow County</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-POPCENTER_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POPCENTER-142">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gilead,_Ohio" title="Mount Gilead, Ohio">Mount Gilead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-POPCEN_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POPCEN-143">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> This is approximately 6,346 feet (1,934&#160;m) south and west of Ohio's population center in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-POPCENTER_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POPCENTER-142">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;-10 to -5 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff0000; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;-5 to -2 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff8080; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;-2 to 0 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#80ff80; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;0 to 2 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#00ff00; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;2 to 5 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#00aa00; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;5 to 10 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#005500; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;10 to 20 percent</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#002b00; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160; More than 20 percent</div> </figcaption></figure>
<p>As of 2011, 27.6% of Ohio's children under the age of 1 belonged to minority groups.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 6.2% of Ohio's population was under five years of age, 23.7% under 18 years of age, and 14.1% were 65 or older; females made up an estimated 51.2% of the population.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="United States Department of Housing and Urban Development">HUD</a>'s 2022 <a href="/wiki/Annual_Homeless_Assessment_Report_to_Congress" title="Annual Homeless Assessment Report to Congress">Annual Homeless Assessment Report</a>, there were an estimated 10,654 <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homeless</a> people in Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Homelessness_in_Ohio" title="Homelessness in Ohio">Homelessness in Ohio</a></div>

<p>In 2010, there were 469,700 foreign-born residents in Ohio, corresponding to 4.1% of the total population. Of these, 229,049 (2.0%) were naturalized <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_United_States" title="Citizenship of the United States">U.S. citizens</a> and 240,699 (2.1%) were not.<sup id="cite_ref-census1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The largest groups were:<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Mexico (54,166), India (50,256), China (34,901), Germany (19,219), Philippines (16,410), United Kingdom (15,917), Canada (14,223), Russia (11,763), South Korea (11,307), and Ukraine (10,681). Though predominantly white, Ohio has large black populations in all major metropolitan areas throughout the state, Ohio has a significant Hispanic population made up of Mexicans in Toledo and Columbus, and Puerto Ricans in Cleveland and Columbus, and also has a significant and diverse Asian population in Columbus.
</p><p>Ancestry groups (which the census defines as not including racial terms) in the state were:<sup id="cite_ref-census1_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> 26.5% <a href="/wiki/German_American" class="mw-redirect" title="German American">German</a>, 14.1% <a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish</a>, 9.0% <a href="/wiki/English_American" class="mw-redirect" title="English American">English</a>, 6.4% <a href="/wiki/Italian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian American">Italian</a>, 3.8% <a href="/wiki/Polish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish American">Polish</a>, 2.5% <a href="/wiki/French_American" class="mw-redirect" title="French American">French</a>, 1.9% <a href="/wiki/Scottish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish American">Scottish</a>, 1.7% <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Ohioans" title="Hungarian Ohioans">Hungarian</a>, 1.6% <a href="/wiki/Dutch_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch American">Dutch</a>, 1.5% <a href="/wiki/Mexican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican American">Mexican</a>, 1.2% <a href="/wiki/Slovak_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak American">Slovak</a>, 1.1% <a href="/wiki/Welsh_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh American">Welsh</a>, and 1.1% <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotch-Irish American">Scotch-Irish</a>. Ancestries claimed by less than 1% of the population include <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan African">Sub-Saharan African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">Puerto Rican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss American">Swiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish American">Swedish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab American">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek American">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian American">Norwegian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian American">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian American">Austrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian American">Lithuanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Finnish American">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indian American">West Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovene_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovene American">Slovene</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Languages">Languages</h3></div>
<p>About 6.7% of the population age 5 years and older reported speaking a language other than English, with 2.2% of the population speaking Spanish, 2.6% speaking other Indo-European languages, 1.1% speaking Asian and Austronesian languages, and 0.8% speaking other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-census1_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census1-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Numerically: 10,100,586 spoke <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">English</a>, 239,229 <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">Spanish</a>, 55,970 <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_the_United_States" title="German language in the United States">German</a>, 38,990 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States" title="Chinese language in the United States">Chinese</a>, 33,125 <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, and 32,019 <a href="/wiki/French_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="French in the United States">French</a>. In addition, 59,881 spoke a <a href="/wiki/Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic language">Slavic language</a> and 42,673 spoke another <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">West Germanic language</a> according to the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Ohio also had the nation's largest population of <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene speakers</a>, second largest of <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak speakers</a>, second largest of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch_language" title="Pennsylvania Dutch language">Pennsylvania Dutch (German) speakers</a>, and the third largest of <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian speakers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</div>
</div></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/170px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/255px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg/340px-Amish_-_On_the_way_to_school_by_Gadjoboy-crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="832" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Amish" title="Amish">Amish</a> children on their way to school</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Public_Religion_Research_Institute" title="Public Religion Research Institute">Public Religion Research Institute</a>'s 2021 <i>American Values Survey</i>, 64% of Ohioans identified as <a href="/wiki/Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian">Christian</a>. Specifically, 19% of Ohio's population identified as <a href="/wiki/Mainline_(Protestant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainline (Protestant)">Mainline Protestant</a>, 17% as <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a>, 7% as <a href="/wiki/Black_church" title="Black church">Historically Black Protestant</a>, and 18% as <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>. Roughly 30% of the population were unaffiliated with any religious body. Small minorities of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jews</a> (2%), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> (1%), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (&lt;1%), <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslims</a> (&lt;1%),  <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> (&lt;1%), <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormons</a> (&lt;1%), and other faiths exist according to this study.<sup id="cite_ref-Values_Atlas_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Values_Atlas-167">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Altogether, those identifying with a religion or spiritual tradition were 70% of the state's population.
</p><p>Per the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a>'s (ARDA) 2020 study, Christianity remained the predominant religion. <a href="/wiki/Nondenominational_Christianity" title="Nondenominational Christianity">Non-denominational Christianity</a>, numbering 1,411,863, were the largest Protestant cohort, although Catholicism remained the single-largest denomination with 1,820,233 adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> According to the ARDA, in 2010 the largest Christian denominations by adherents were the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> with 1,992,567; the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> with 496,232; the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">Evangelical Lutheran Church in America</a> with 223,253, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> with 171,000, the Christian Churches and Churches of Christ with 141,311, the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Christ" title="United Church of Christ">United Church of Christ</a> with 118,000, and the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">Presbyterian Church (USA)</a> with 110,000.<sup id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-169">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> With about 80,000 adherents in 2020, Ohio had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_Amish_population" title="List of U.S. states by Amish population">second largest Amish population</a> of all U.S. states, only behind neighboring <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Elizabethtown_College,_the_Young_Center_for_Anabaptist_and_Pietist_Studies_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elizabethtown_College,_the_Young_Center_for_Anabaptist_and_Pietist_Studies-170">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a <a href="/wiki/Pew_Forum" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Forum">Pew Forum</a> poll in 2014, a majority of Ohioans, 56%, felt religion was "very important", 25% that it was "somewhat important", and 19% that religion was "not too important/not important at all". Among them, 38% of Ohioans indicate that they attend religious services at least once weekly, 32% occasionally, and 30% seldom or never.<sup id="cite_ref-pew2014_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew2014-171">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ohio" title="Economy of Ohio">Economy of Ohio</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ohio_locations_by_per_capita_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio locations by per capita income">Ohio locations by per capita income</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/170px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/255px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg/340px-Cincinnati-procter-and-gamble-headquarters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a><figcaption>Cincinnati's <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> is one of Ohio's largest companies in terms of revenue.</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>, the total number of people employed in 2016 was 4,790,178. The total number of unique employer establishments was 252,201, while the total number of non-employer establishments was 785,833.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Ohio was ranked second in the country for best business climate by Site Selection magazine, based on a business-activity database.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The state has also won three consecutive Governor's Cup awards from the magazine, based on business growth and developments.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Ohio's gross domestic product (GDP) was $626&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> This ranks Ohio's economy as the seventh-largest among all 50 states and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Small Business &amp; Entrepreneurship Council ranked the state No. 10 for best business-friendly tax systems in their Business Tax Index 2009, including a top corporate tax and capital gains rate that were both ranked No. 6 at 1.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-SMEC_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMEC-177">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Ohio was ranked No. 11 by the council for best friendly-policy states according to their Small Business Survival Index 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The Directorship's Boardroom Guide ranked the state No. 13 overall for best business climate, including No. 7 for best litigation climate.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Forbes ranked the state No. 8 for best regulatory environment in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Ohio has five of the top 115 colleges in the nation, according to <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 2010 rankings,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and was ranked No. 8 by the same magazine in 2008 for best high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ohio's <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> stands at 4.5% as of February 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> down from 10.7% in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The state still lacks 45,000 jobs compared to the pre-<a href="/wiki/Great_Recession_in_the_United_States" title="Great Recession in the United States">recession</a> numbers of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-perkins_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perkins-186">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The labor force participation as of April 2015 is 63%, slightly above the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-perkins_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perkins-186">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> As of 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Ohio's per capita income was $60,402, ranking 38th in the U.S., and the state's <a href="/wiki/Median_household_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Median household income">median household income</a> was $65,720.<sup id="cite_ref-r095_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r095-187">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-u858_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u858-188">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2023, 13.4% of the population was living below the poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial industry">financial activities</a> sectors each compose 18.3% of Ohio's GDP, making them Ohio's largest industries by percentage of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Ohio has the third largest manufacturing workforce behind California and Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Ohio has the largest bioscience sector in the Midwest, and is a national leader in the "green" economy. Ohio is the largest producer in the country of plastics, rubber, fabricated metals, electrical equipment, and appliances.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> 5,212,000 Ohioans are currently employed by wage or salary.<sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By employment, Ohio's largest sector is trade/transportation/utilities, which employs 1,010,000 Ohioans, or 19.4% of Ohio's workforce, while the <a href="/wiki/Health_care_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care industry">health care</a> and education sector employs 825,000 Ohioans (15.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Government employs 787,000 Ohioans (15.1%), manufacturing employs 669,000 Ohioans (12.9%), and professional and technical services employs 638,000 Ohioans (12.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Ohio's manufacturing sector is the third-largest of all fifty United States states in terms of gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-DDOH_176-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOH-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Fifty-nine of the United States' top 1,000 publicly traded companies (by revenue in 2008) are headquartered in Ohio, including <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_%26_Rubber" class="mw-redirect" title="Goodyear Tire &amp; Rubber">Goodyear Tire &amp; Rubber</a>, <a href="/wiki/AK_Steel" title="AK Steel">AK Steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timken_Company" title="Timken Company">Timken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abercrombie_%26_Fitch" title="Abercrombie &amp; Fitch">Abercrombie &amp; Fitch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy&#39;s">Wendy's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CORPLIST_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CORPLIST-193">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ohio is also one of 41 states with its own lottery,<sup id="cite_ref-LOTTO_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOTTO-194">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Lottery" title="Ohio Lottery">Ohio Lottery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LOTTO2_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOTTO2-195">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ohio&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Ohio Lottery has contributed more than $26 billion to education beginning in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Income_inequality" class="mw-redirect" title="Income inequality">Income inequality</a> in Ohio, both before and after taxes, has risen significantly since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Ohio's overall income grew in Ohio from 2009 to 2012, with an overall 7.1% increase in income growth. The top 1% had a 37.0% in income growth, while the bottom 99% grew their income by only 2.3%. The top 1% accounted for 71.9% of the overall shared income during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The burden of <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> falls disproportionately on lower-income <a href="/wiki/Tax_bracket" title="Tax bracket">tax brackets</a>. In 2018, the bottom 20% of earners contributed 12.3% of their income towards various taxes, while the top 1% only paid 6.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png/220px-Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png/330px-Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png/440px-Map_of_Ohio_showing_Interurban_Railways_c_1907.png 2x" data-file-width="1385" data-file-height="1939" /></a><figcaption>Map of Ohio showing Interurban Railways <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1907</span></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_welcome_sign_(2019).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg/220px-Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg/330px-Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg/440px-Ohio_welcome_sign_%282019%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2770" data-file-height="1870" /></a><figcaption>Ohio welcome sign in 2019</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Roads">Roads</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Interstate_Highways_in_Ohio" title="List of Interstate Highways in Ohio">List of Interstate Highways in Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._Routes_in_Ohio" title="List of U.S. Routes in Ohio">List of U.S. Routes in Ohio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_state_routes_in_Ohio" title="List of state routes in Ohio">List of state routes in Ohio</a></div>
<p>Many major east–west transportation corridors go through Ohio. One of those pioneer routes, known in the early 20th century as "Main Market Route 3", was chosen in 1913 to become part of the historic <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Highway" title="Lincoln Highway">Lincoln Highway</a> which was the first road across America, connecting New York City to San Francisco. In Ohio, the Lincoln Highway linked many towns and cities together, including <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">Canton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Ohio" title="Mansfield, Ohio">Mansfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wooster,_Ohio" title="Wooster, Ohio">Wooster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Ohio" title="Lima, Ohio">Lima</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Van_Wert,_Ohio" title="Van Wert, Ohio">Van Wert</a>. The Lincoln Highway's arrival in Ohio was a major influence on the state's development. Upon the advent of the federal numbered highway system in 1926, the Lincoln Highway through Ohio became <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_30_in_Ohio" title="U.S. Route 30 in Ohio">U.S. Route 30</a>.
</p><p>Ohio is home to 228 miles (367&#160;km) of the <a href="/wiki/National_Road" title="National Road">National Road</a>, now <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 40 in Ohio">U.S. Route 40</a>.
</p><p>Ohio has a highly developed network of roads and interstate highways. Major east-west through routes include the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Turnpike" title="Ohio Turnpike">Ohio Turnpike</a> (<a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 80 in Ohio">I-80</a>/<a href="/wiki/Interstate_90_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 90 in Ohio">I-90</a>) in the north, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_76_in_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 76 in Ohio">I-76</a> through <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">Akron</a> to <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 70 in Ohio">I-70</a> through <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Highway_(Ohio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Appalachian Highway (Ohio)">Appalachian Highway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Route_32" title="Ohio State Route 32">State Route 32</a>) running from <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>. Major north–south routes include <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 75 in Ohio">I-75</a> in the west through <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo</a>, Dayton, and Cincinnati, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_71" title="Interstate 71">I-71</a> through the middle of the state from <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> through Columbus and Cincinnati into <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_77_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 77 in Ohio">I-77</a> in the eastern part of the state from Cleveland through Akron, <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">Canton</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Philadelphia,_Ohio" title="New Philadelphia, Ohio">New Philadelphia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marietta,_Ohio" title="Marietta, Ohio">Marietta</a> south into West Virginia. Interstate 75 between Cincinnati and Dayton is one of Ohio's most heavily traveled sections of interstate.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Trails">Trails</h3></div>
<p>Ohio has a highly developed network of signed state bicycle routes. Many of them follow <a href="/wiki/Rail_trail" title="Rail trail">rail trails</a>, with conversion ongoing. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_to_Erie_Trail" title="Ohio to Erie Trail">Ohio to Erie Trail</a> (route 1) connects Cincinnati, Columbus, and Cleveland. <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bicycle_Route_50" title="U.S. Bicycle Route 50">U.S. Bicycle Route 50</a> traverses Ohio from <a href="/wiki/Steubenville,_Ohio" title="Steubenville, Ohio">Steubenville</a> to the Indiana state line outside <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Indiana" title="Richmond, Indiana">Richmond</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USRN_USBR_50_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USRN_USBR_50-200">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ohio has several long-distance hiking trails, the most prominent of which is the <a href="/wiki/Buckeye_Trail" title="Buckeye Trail">Buckeye Trail</a>, which extends 1,444&#160;mi (2,324&#160;km) in a loop around the state. Part of it is on roads and part on wooded trail. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/North_Country_Trail" title="North Country Trail">North Country Trail</a> (the longest of the 11 <a href="/wiki/National_Scenic_Trail" class="mw-redirect" title="National Scenic Trail">National Scenic Trails</a> authorized by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/American_Discovery_Trail" title="American Discovery Trail">American Discovery Trail</a> (a system of recreational trails and roads that collectively form a coast-to-coast route across the mid-tier of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>) pass through Ohio. Much of these two trails coincide with the Buckeye Trail.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Rail">Rail</h3></div>
