</td></tr></tbody></table>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_railroads" title="List of Ohio railroads">List of Ohio railroads</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ohio_train_stations" title="List of Ohio train stations">List of Ohio train stations</a></div>
<p>Ohio has an extensive rail network, though today most lines carry only freight traffic. Three <a href="/wiki/Class_I_railroads" class="mw-redirect" title="Class I railroads">Class I</a> freight railroads operate in Ohio: <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">Norfolk Southern Railway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Railway" title="Canadian National Railway">Canadian National Railway</a>. Many local freight carriers also exist in the state.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, the national passenger railroad, operates three long-distance rail routes through Ohio. The <i><a href="/wiki/Lake_Shore_Limited" title="Lake Shore Limited">Lake Shore Limited</a></i> serves <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Lakefront_Station" title="Cleveland Lakefront Station">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elyria_station" title="Elyria station">Elyria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr._Plaza_(Toledo)" title="Martin Luther King Jr. Plaza (Toledo)">Toledo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandusky_station" title="Sandusky station">Sandusky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_station_(Ohio)" title="Bryan station (Ohio)">Bryan</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Capitol_Limited" title="Capitol Limited">Capitol Limited</a></i> stops in those cities as well as in <a href="/wiki/Alliance_station" title="Alliance station">Alliance</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(train)" title="Cardinal (train)">Cardinal</a></i> serves <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Union_Terminal" title="Cincinnati Union Terminal">Cincinnati Union Terminal</a>. From Ohio, passengers can ride directly to <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Union_Station" title="Chicago Union Station">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Penn_Station" title="New York Penn Station">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Union_Station" title="Washington Union Station">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Union_Station" title="Indianapolis Union Station">Indianapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Pittsburgh)" title="Union Station (Pittsburgh)">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo%E2%80%93Depew_station" title="Buffalo–Depew station">Buffalo</a>, and dozens of destinations in-between.
</p><p>Columbus is the largest city in the U.S. with no passenger rail. Its <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Columbus,_Ohio)" title="Union Station (Columbus, Ohio)">Union Station</a> was last served in 1979 by the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Limited_(Amtrak_train)" title="National Limited (Amtrak train)">National Limited</a>.</i>
</p><p>Ohio is home to several <a href="/wiki/Heritage_railway" title="Heritage railway">scenic railways</a> and museums, including the <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Valley_Scenic_Railroad" title="Cuyahoga Valley Scenic Railroad">Cuyahoga Valley Scenic Railroad</a> through <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Valley_National_Park" title="Cuyahoga Valley National Park">Cuyahoga Valley National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Steam_Roundhouse" title="Age of Steam Roundhouse">Age of Steam Roundhouse</a> museum, and the <a href="/wiki/Hocking_Valley_Scenic_Railway" title="Hocking Valley Scenic Railway">Hocking Valley Scenic Railway</a> near <a href="/wiki/Hocking_Hills_State_Park" title="Hocking Hills State Park">Hocking Hills State Park</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Transit">Transit</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg/220px-Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg/330px-Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg/440px-Cincinnati-bell-connector_station-1-the-banks_09-11-2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2928" data-file-height="1892" /></a><figcaption>Cincinnati <a href="/wiki/Connector_(Cincinnati)" title="Connector (Cincinnati)">Connector</a> <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">streetcar</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Mass transit exists in many forms in Ohio cities, primarily through bus systems. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cleveland_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Greater Cleveland Regional Transit Authority">Greater Cleveland Regional Transit Authority</a> (GCRTA) operates the <a href="/wiki/RTA_Rapid_Transit" title="RTA Rapid Transit">RTA Rapid Transit</a> system, which consists of one heavy rail line, three <a href="/wiki/Light_rail_in_the_United_States" title="Light rail in the United States">light rail</a> lines, and three <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> lines. Cincinnati is served by the <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Ohio_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Southwest Ohio Regional Transit Authority">Southwest Ohio Regional Transit Authority</a> (SORTA) bus network as well as a 3.6-mile (5.8&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Streetcar" class="mw-redirect" title="Streetcar">streetcar</a> line, the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bell_Connector" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati Bell Connector">Cincinnati Bell Connector</a>. Other major transit agencies in Ohio include the <a href="/wiki/Central_Ohio_Transit_Authority" title="Central Ohio Transit Authority">Central Ohio Transit Authority</a> (COTA) serving Columbus and the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Dayton_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Greater Dayton Regional Transit Authority">Greater Dayton Regional Transit Authority</a> (GDRTA) serving Dayton.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Air_travel">Air travel</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Ohio" title="List of airports in Ohio">List of airports in Ohio</a></div>
<p>Ohio has four international airports, four commercial, and two military. The four international include <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland Hopkins International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Glenn_Columbus_International_Airport" title="John Glenn Columbus International Airport">John Glenn Columbus International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayton_International_Airport" title="Dayton International Airport">Dayton International Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_International_Airport" title="Rickenbacker International Airport">Rickenbacker International Airport</a> (one of two military airfields). The other military airfield is <a href="/wiki/Wright_Patterson_Air_Force_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Wright Patterson Air Force Base">Wright Patterson Air Force Base</a> which is one of the largest Air Force bases in the United States. Other major airports are in <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Express_Airport" title="Toledo Express Airport">Toledo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akron-Canton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Akron-Canton Airport">Akron</a>. Cincinnati's main airport, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati/Northern_Kentucky_International_Airport" title="Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport">Cincinnati/Northern Kentucky International Airport</a>, is in <a href="/wiki/Hebron,_Kentucky" title="Hebron, Kentucky">Hebron, Kentucky</a>, and therefore is not included in Ohio airport lists.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Waterways">Waterways</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Ohio" title="List of rivers of Ohio">List of rivers of Ohio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Historic_Ohio_Canals" title="Historic Ohio Canals">Historic Ohio Canals</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Law_and_government">Law and government</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ohio" title="Government of Ohio">Government of Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg/170px-Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg/255px-Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg/340px-Gov-Mike-DeWine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3735" data-file-height="4686" /></a><figcaption>Current governor <a href="/wiki/Mike_DeWine" title="Mike DeWine">Mike DeWine</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The state government of Ohio consists of the executive, legislative, and judicial branches.<sup id="cite_ref-CO_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CO-201">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The political culture of Ohio has been described as <a href="/wiki/Political_moderate" title="Political moderate">moderate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-204">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</h3></div>
<p>The executive branch is headed by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Ohio">governor of Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CO_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CO-201">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The current governor is <a href="/wiki/Mike_DeWine" title="Mike DeWine">Mike DeWine</a> since 2019, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GOV_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOV-205">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Ohio" title="Lieutenant Governor of Ohio">lieutenant governor</a> succeeds the governor in the event of any removal from office, and performs any duties assigned by the governor.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The current lieutenant governor is <a href="/wiki/Jon_Husted" title="Jon Husted">Jon Husted</a>. The other elected constitutional offices in the executive branch are the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Secretary_of_State" title="Ohio Secretary of State">secretary of state</a> (<a href="/wiki/Frank_LaRose" title="Frank LaRose">Frank LaRose</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Auditor" title="Ohio State Auditor">auditor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Keith_Faber" title="Keith Faber">Keith Faber</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Treasurer" title="Ohio State Treasurer">treasurer</a> (<a href="/wiki/Robert_Sprague" title="Robert Sprague">Robert Sprague</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Attorney_General" title="Ohio Attorney General">attorney general</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dave_Yost" title="Dave Yost">Dave Yost</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-CO_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CO-201">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> There are 21 state administrative departments in the executive branch.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg/220px-Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg/330px-Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg/440px-Ohio_Statehouse_exterior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4869" data-file-height="3052" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Statehouse" title="Ohio Statehouse">Ohio Statehouse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_General_Assembly" title="Ohio General Assembly">Ohio General Assembly</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_General_Assembly" title="Ohio General Assembly">Ohio General Assembly</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> legislature consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Senate" title="Ohio Senate">Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_House_of_Representatives" title="Ohio House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The Senate is composed of 33 districts, each of which is represented by one senator. Each senator represents approximately 330,000 <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">constituents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The House of Representatives has 99 members.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> is the majority party in both houses as of the <a href="/wiki/2022_Ohio_elections" title="2022 Ohio elections">2022 election cycle</a>.
</p><p>In order to be enacted into law, a bill must be adopted by both houses of the General Assembly and signed by the governor. If the governor vetoes a bill, the General Assembly can override the veto with a three-fifths supermajority of both houses. A bill will also become a law if the governor fails to sign or veto it within 10 days of its being presented. The <a href="/wiki/Session_laws" title="Session laws">session laws</a> are published in the official <i><a href="/wiki/Law_of_Ohio" title="Law of Ohio">Law of Ohio</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen199731–32_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen199731–32-213">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> These in turn have been <a href="/wiki/Codification_(law)" title="Codification (law)">codified</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Ohio_Revised_Code" title="Ohio Revised Code">Ohio Revised Code</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen199765–66_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen199765–66-214">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The General Assembly, with the approval of the governor, draws the U.S. congressional district lines for Ohio's 16 seats in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Apportionment_Board" title="Ohio Apportionment Board">Ohio Apportionment Board</a> draws state legislative district lines in Ohio.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg/220px-Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg/330px-Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg/440px-Ohio_State_Office_Building_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Moyer_Ohio_Judicial_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas J. Moyer Ohio Judicial Center">Thomas J. Moyer Ohio Judicial Center</a> holds the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Ohio" title="Supreme Court of Ohio">Supreme Court of Ohio</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>There are three levels of the Ohio state <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a>. The lowest is the court of common pleas: each county maintains its own constitutionally mandated court of common pleas, which maintain jurisdiction over "all justiciable matters".<sup id="cite_ref-District_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-District-215">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The intermediate-level court system is the district court system.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Twelve courts of appeals exist, each retaining jurisdiction over appeals from common pleas, municipal, and county courts in a set geographical area.<sup id="cite_ref-District_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-District-215">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> A case heard in this system is decided by a three-judge panel, and each judge is elected.<sup id="cite_ref-District_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-District-215">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state's highest-ranking court is the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio Supreme Court">Ohio Supreme Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SCOO_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCOO-217">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> A seven-justice panel composes the court, which, by its own <a href="/wiki/Certiorari#State_courts" title="Certiorari">discretion</a>, hears appeals from the courts of appeals, and retains original jurisdiction over limited matters.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Local_government">Local government</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Ohio" title="List of counties in Ohio">List of counties in Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Ohio" title="List of municipalities in Ohio">List of municipalities in Ohio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_townships_in_Ohio" title="List of townships in Ohio">List of townships in Ohio</a></div>
<p>There are also several levels of local government in Ohio: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Ohio" title="List of counties in Ohio">counties</a>, municipalities (<a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Ohio">cities</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_villages_in_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="List of villages in Ohio">villages</a>), <a href="/wiki/List_of_townships_in_Ohio" title="List of townships in Ohio">townships</a>, special districts, and school districts.
</p><p>Ohio is divided into 88 counties.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Ohio law defines a structure for county government, although they may adopt charters for home rule.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997&#91;httpsarchiveorgdetailsohiolegalresearc0000putnpage106_106&#93;–114_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsohiolegalresearc0000putnpage106_106]–114-221">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Summit_County,_Ohio" title="Summit County, Ohio">Summit County</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County,_Ohio" title="Cuyahoga County, Ohio">Cuyahoga County</a><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> have chosen an alternate form of government. The other counties have a government with a three-member board of county commissioners,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> a sheriff,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> coroner,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> auditor,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> treasurer,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> clerk of the court of common pleas<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> prosecutor,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> engineer,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and recorder.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are two kinds of incorporated municipalities, 251 cities and 681 villages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ohio_Secretary_of_State_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ohio_Secretary_of_State-232">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> If a municipality has five thousand or more residents as of the last <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Census">United States Census</a> it is a city, otherwise it is a village.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Municipalities have full home rule powers, may adopt a charter, ordinances and resolutions for self-government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997106–114_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997106–114-235">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Each municipality chooses its own form of government, but most have elected mayors and city councils or city commissions. City governments provide much more extensive services than county governments, such as police forces and paid (as opposed to volunteer) fire departments.
</p><p>The entire area of the state is encompassed by townships.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> When the boundaries of a township are coterminous with the boundaries of a city or village, the township ceases to exist as a separate government (called a <a href="/wiki/Paper_township" title="Paper township">paper township</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Townships are governed by a three-member board of township trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Townships may have limited home rule powers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997110–111_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPutnamSchaefgen1997110–111-236">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are more than 600 city, local, and exempted village school districts providing K-12 education in Ohio, as well as about four dozen joint vocation school districts, which are separate from the K-12 districts. Each city school district, local school district, or exempted village school district is governed by an elected board of education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> A school district previously under state supervision (municipal school district) may be governed by a board whose members either are elected or appointed by the mayor of the municipality containing the greatest portion of the district's area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECensus2007235_220-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECensus2007235-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Politics">Politics</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ohio" title="Politics of Ohio">Politics of Ohio</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Ohio" title="Elections in Ohio">Elections in Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Ohio" title="Political party strength in Ohio">Political party strength in Ohio</a></div>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;Mother_of_presidents&quot;"><span id=".22Mother_of_presidents.22"></span>"Mother of presidents"</h3></div>
<p>Six U.S. presidents hailed from Ohio at the time of their elections, giving rise to its nickname "mother of presidents", a sobriquet it shares with <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. It is also termed "modern mother of presidents", in contrast to Virginia's status as the origin of presidents earlier in American history. Seven presidents were born in Ohio, making it second to Virginia's eight. Virginia-born <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a> lived most of his life in Ohio and is also buried there. Harrison conducted his political career while living on the family compound, founded by his father-in-law, <a href="/wiki/John_Cleves_Symmes" title="John Cleves Symmes">John Cleves Symmes</a>, in <a href="/wiki/North_Bend,_Ohio" title="North Bend, Ohio">North Bend, Ohio</a>. The seven presidents born in Ohio were <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> (elected from <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>), <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">Rutherford B. Hayes</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison" title="Benjamin Harrison">Benjamin Harrison</a> (grandson of William Henry Harrison &amp; elected from <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>), <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">Warren G. Harding</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HEINRICHS_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEINRICHS-238">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> All seven were <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Republican_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the United States Republican Party">Republicans</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electoral_history">Electoral history</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg/220px-Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg/330px-Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg/440px-Ohio_Presidential_Election_Results_2020.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="810" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election_in_Ohio" title="2020 United States presidential election in Ohio">Presidential election results</a> by county for 2020 <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend" style="text-align:left;"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#4389E3; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&#160;</span>&#160;Democratic</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend" style="text-align:left;"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#AA0000; color:white; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&#160;</span>&#160;Republican</div></figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio has been considered a <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a>, being won by either the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> candidates reasonably each election. As such, it is usually targeted by both major-party campaigns, especially in competitive elections.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Pivotal in the election of <a href="/wiki/1888_United_States_presidential_election" title="1888 United States presidential election">1888</a>, Ohio has been a regular swing state since 1980 and considered a <a href="/wiki/Bellwether" title="Bellwether">bellwether</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> This status was called into question after incumbent Republican <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> won the state by an eight-point margin in the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election" title="2020 United States presidential election">2020 presidential election</a> despite losing nationally to Democratic challenger <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian R. Douglas Hurt asserts that not since Virginia "had a state made such a mark on national political affairs".<sup id="cite_ref-holli162_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holli162-243">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> notes that "This slice of the mid-west contains a bit of everything American—part north-eastern and part southern, part urban and part rural, part hardscrabble poverty and part booming suburb".<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Since <a href="/wiki/1896_United_States_presidential_election" title="1896 United States presidential election">1896</a>, Ohio has had only three misses in the general election (<a href="/wiki/1944_United_States_presidential_election" title="1944 United States presidential election">Thomas E. Dewey in 1944</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">Richard Nixon in 1960</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election" title="2020 United States presidential election">Donald Trump in 2020</a>) and had the longest perfect streak of any state, voting for the winning presidential candidate in each election from <a href="/wiki/1964_United_States_presidential_election" title="1964 United States presidential election">1964</a> to <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016</a>, and in 33 of the 38 held since the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>. No Republican has ever won the presidency without winning Ohio.
</p><p>As of 2019, there are more than 7.8&#160;million registered Ohioan voters, with 1.3&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Democratic_Party" title="Ohio Democratic Party">Democrats</a> and 1.9&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Republican_Party" title="Ohio Republican Party">Republicans</a>. They are disproportionate in age, with a million more over 65 than there are 18- to 24-year-olds.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_elections" title="2010 United States elections">2010 midterm elections</a>, Ohio's voter demographic has leaned towards the Republican Party.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The governor, <a href="/wiki/Mike_DeWine" title="Mike DeWine">Mike DeWine</a>, is Republican, as are all other non-judicial statewide elected officials, including Lieutenant Governor <a href="/wiki/Jon_A._Husted" class="mw-redirect" title="Jon A. Husted">Jon A. Husted</a>, Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Dave_Yost" title="Dave Yost">Dave Yost</a>, State Auditor <a href="/wiki/Keith_Faber" title="Keith Faber">Keith Faber</a>, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Frank_LaRose" title="Frank LaRose">Frank LaRose</a> and State Treasurer <a href="/wiki/Robert_Sprague" title="Robert Sprague">Robert Sprague</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Senate" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio State Senate">Ohio State Senate</a> the Republicans are the majority, 25–8, and in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_House_of_Representatives" title="Ohio House of Representatives">Ohio House of Representatives</a> the Republicans control the delegation 64–35.
</p><p>Losing one seat in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a> following the 2020 census, Ohio has 15 seats for the two presidential elections of the decade in 2024 and 2028.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/2022_Ohio_elections" title="2022 Ohio elections">2022 cycle</a>, ten federal representatives are Republicans while five are Democrats. <a href="/wiki/Marcy_Kaptur" title="Marcy Kaptur">Marcy Kaptur</a> (D-<a href="/wiki/Ohio%27s_9th_congressional_district" title="Ohio&#39;s 9th congressional district">09</a>) is the most senior member of the Ohio delegation to the U.S. House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Seniority_in_the_United_States_Senate" title="Seniority in the United States Senate">senior U.S. senator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherrod_Brown" title="Sherrod Brown">Sherrod Brown</a>, is a Democrat, while the junior, <a href="/wiki/JD_Vance" title="JD Vance">JD Vance</a>, is a Republican.<sup id="cite_ref-elections.nytimes.com_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elections.nytimes.com-249">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Allegations_of_voter_suppression">Allegations of voter suppression</h3></div>
<p>Since 1994, the state has had a policy of purging infrequent voters from its rolls. In April 2016, a lawsuit was filed, challenging this policy on the grounds that it violated the <a href="/wiki/National_Voter_Registration_Act_of_1993" title="National Voter Registration Act of 1993">National Voter Registration Act (NVRA) of 1993</a><sup id="cite_ref-aclu-husted_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aclu-husted-251">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Help_America_Vote_Act_of_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Help America Vote Act of 2002">Help America Vote Act of 2002</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic-husted_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-husted-252">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> In June, the federal district court ruled for the plaintiffs and entered a preliminary injunction applicable only to the November 2016 election. The preliminary injunction was upheld in September by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Sixth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Sixth Circuit">Court of Appeals for the Sixth Circuit</a>. Had it not been upheld, thousands of voters would have been purged from the rolls just a few weeks before the election.<sup id="cite_ref-aclu-husted_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aclu-husted-251">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was estimated in 2017 that the state has removed up to two million voters since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2022)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In a 2020 study, Ohio was ranked as the 17th hardest state for citizens to vote in.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ohio" title="Education in Ohio">Education in Ohio</a></div>
<p>Ohio's system of <a href="/wiki/Public_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Public education">public education</a> is outlined in Article VI of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio Constitution">state constitution</a>, and in Title XXXIII of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Revised_Code" title="Ohio Revised Code">Ohio Revised Code</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ohio_University" title="Ohio University">Ohio University</a>, the first university in the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>, was also the first public institution in Ohio. Substantively, Ohio's system is similar to those found in <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">other states</a>. At the State level, the Ohio Department of Education, which is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Board_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio State Board of Education">Ohio State Board of Education</a>, governs primary and secondary educational institutions. At the municipal level, there are approximately 700 school districts statewide. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Board_of_Regents" title="Ohio Board of Regents">Ohio Board of Regents</a> coordinates and assists with Ohio's institutions of higher education which have recently been reorganized into the <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Ohio" title="University System of Ohio">University System of Ohio</a> under Governor Strickland. The system averages an annual enrollment of more than 400,000 students, making it one of the five largest state university systems in the U.S.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Ohio" title="List of colleges and universities in Ohio">List of colleges and universities in Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg/220px-Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg/330px-Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg/440px-Ohio-Columbus-University-Hall-2017-10-21-001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5871" data-file-height="3914" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/University_Hall_(Ohio_State_University)" title="University Hall (Ohio State University)">University Hall</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a> in Columbus, Ohio's largest university by enrollment.<sup id="cite_ref-headcount_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-headcount-256">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio is home to several public and private institutions of higher learning. Prior to statehood, the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Ordinance" title="Northwest Ordinance">Northwest Ordinance</a> of 1787 included a provision to establish an institution of higher education in the region, which resulted in the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Ohio_University" title="Ohio University">Ohio University</a> in 1804 as Ohio's first college.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ohio schools consistently ranking in the top 50 nationally of the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> of liberal arts colleges include members of the “<a href="/wiki/Five_Colleges_of_Ohio" title="Five Colleges of Ohio">Five Colleges of Ohio</a>”: <a href="/wiki/Denison_University" title="Denison University">Denison University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenyon_College" title="Kenyon College">Kenyon College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin College</a>. Ranking in the top 100 of national research universities typically includes <a href="/wiki/Case_Western_Reserve_University" title="Case Western Reserve University">Case Western Reserve University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami_University" title="Miami University">Miami University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>13 state universities
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green_State_University" title="Bowling Green State University">Bowling Green State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green,_Ohio" title="Bowling Green, Ohio">Bowling Green</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_State_University" title="Central State University">Central State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wilberforce,_Ohio" title="Wilberforce, Ohio">Wilberforce</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleveland_State_University" title="Cleveland State University">Cleveland State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kent_State_University" title="Kent State University">Kent State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kent,_Ohio" title="Kent, Ohio">Kent</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miami_University" title="Miami University">Miami University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oxford,_Ohio" title="Oxford, Ohio">Oxford</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ohio_University" title="Ohio University">Ohio University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Athens,_Ohio" title="Athens, Ohio">Athens</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shawnee_State_University" title="Shawnee State University">Shawnee State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Ohio" title="Portsmouth, Ohio">Portsmouth</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Akron" title="University of Akron">University of Akron</a> (<a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">Akron</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Cincinnati" title="University of Cincinnati">University of Cincinnati</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Toledo" title="University of Toledo">University of Toledo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wright_State_University" title="Wright State University">Wright State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dayton" class="mw-redirect" title="Dayton">Dayton</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Youngstown_State_University" title="Youngstown State University">Youngstown State University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio" title="Youngstown, Ohio">Youngstown</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li>24 state university branch and regional campuses</li></ul>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg/220px-Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg/330px-Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg/440px-Oberlin_College_-_Bosworth_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>Bosworth Hall at <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin College</a> in northeast Ohio, the first college in the U.S. to admit women<sup id="cite_ref-Jones-WilsonAsbury1996_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-WilsonAsbury1996-261">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<ul><li>46 private colleges and universities</li>
<li>6 free-standing state-assisted <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical schools</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Boonshoft_School_of_Medicine" title="Boonshoft School of Medicine">Boonshoft School of Medicine</a>, Wright State University</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heritage_College_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Heritage College of Osteopathic Medicine">Heritage College of Osteopathic Medicine</a>, Ohio University</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio_Medical_University" title="Northeast Ohio Medical University">Northeast Ohio Medical University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OSU_College_of_Medicine_and_Public_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="OSU College of Medicine and Public Health">The Ohio State University College of Medicine and Public Health</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Cincinnati_Academic_Health_Center#University_of_Cincinnati_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Cincinnati Academic Health Center">University of Cincinnati College of Medicine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Toledo_Medical_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Toledo Medical Center">University of Toledo College of Medicine</a> (formerly Medical University of Ohio)</li></ul></li>
<li>15 community colleges</li>
<li>8 technical colleges</li>
<li>24 independent non-profit colleges</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Libraries">Libraries</h3></div>
<p>Ohio is home to some of the nation's highest-ranked public libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-haplr_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haplr-262">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hennen%27s_American_Public_Library_Ratings" class="mw-redirect" title="Hennen&#39;s American Public Library Ratings">2008 study by Thomas J. Hennen Jr.</a> ranked Ohio as number one in a state-by-state comparison.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> For 2008, 31 of Ohio's library systems were all ranked in the top ten for American cities of their population category.<sup id="cite_ref-haplr_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haplr-262">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>500,000 books or more
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Columbus_Metropolitan_Library" title="Columbus Metropolitan Library">Columbus Metropolitan Library</a> (First)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County_Public_Library" title="Cuyahoga County Public Library">Cuyahoga County Public Library</a> (Second)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Public_Library_of_Cincinnati_and_Hamilton_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Library of Cincinnati and Hamilton County">Public Library of Cincinnati and Hamilton County</a> (Tenth)</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Public_Library_Information_Network_(OPLIN)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio Public Library Information Network (OPLIN)">Ohio Public Library Information Network (OPLIN)</a> is an organization that provides Ohio residents with internet access to their 251 public libraries. OPLIN also provides Ohioans with free home access to high-quality, subscription research databases.
</p><p>Ohio also offers the <a href="/wiki/OhioLINK" title="OhioLINK">OhioLINK</a> program, allowing Ohio's libraries (particularly those from colleges and universities) access to materials for the other libraries. The program is largely successful in allowing researchers for access to books and other media that might not be otherwise available.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arts">Arts</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Music">Music</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ohio" title="Music of Ohio">Music of Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_hall_at_night.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rock_hall_at_night.jpg/220px-Rock_hall_at_night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rock_hall_at_night.jpg/330px-Rock_hall_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rock_hall_at_night.jpg/440px-Rock_hall_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2160" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in Cleveland</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_Blues_Music_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhythm and Blues Music Hall of Fame">Rhythm and Blues Music Hall of Fame</a> are both located in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>. Cleveland <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">disc jockey</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Freed" title="Alan Freed">Alan Freed</a> is credited with coining the term and promoting <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> in the early 1950s. <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/American_Classical_Music_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="American Classical Music Hall of Fame and Museum">American Classical Music Hall of Fame and Museum</a>. Six Ohio musicians are Rock and Roll Hall of Fame members, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl" title="Dave Grohl">Dave Grohl</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nirvana" title="Nirvana">Nirvana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>), <a href="/wiki/The_Isley_Brothers" title="The Isley Brothers">the Isley Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">Nine Inch Nails</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Womack" title="Bobby Womack">Bobby Womack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Orr" title="Benjamin Orr">Benjamin Orr</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Cars" title="The Cars">The Cars</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde" title="Chrissie Hynde">Chrissie Hynde</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Pretenders" title="The Pretenders">The Pretenders</a>). Also inducted was disk jockey <a href="/wiki/Alan_Freed" title="Alan Freed">Alan Freed</a>.
</p><p>Other popular musicians from Ohio include <a href="/wiki/Mamie_Smith" title="Mamie Smith">Mamie Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dean_Martin" title="Dean Martin">Dean Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Joseph" title="Tyler Joseph">Tyler Joseph</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Dun" title="Josh Dun">Josh Dun</a> of <a href="/wiki/Twenty_One_Pilots" title="Twenty One Pilots">Twenty One Pilots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Yankovic" title="Frankie Yankovic">Frankie Yankovic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doris_Day" title="Doris Day">Doris Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_McGuire_Sisters" title="The McGuire Sisters">the McGuire Sisters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hewett" title="Howard Hewett">Howard Hewett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Murdock" title="Shirley Murdock">Shirley Murdock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boz_Scaggs" title="Boz Scaggs">Boz Scaggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson" title="Marilyn Manson">Marilyn Manson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starset" title="Starset">Starset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Auerbach" title="Dan Auerbach">Dan Auerbach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Carney" title="Patrick Carney">Patrick Carney</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Keys" title="The Black Keys">the Black Keys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Griffin_Layne" title="Griffin Layne">Griffin Layne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Dolce" title="Joe Dolce">Joe Dolce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Cudi" title="Kid Cudi">Kid Cudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_%22Bootsy%22_Collins" class="mw-redirect" title="William &quot;Bootsy&quot; Collins">William "Bootsy" Collins</a>, Stephanie Eulinberg of <a href="/wiki/Kid_Rock" title="Kid Rock">Kid Rock</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Twisted_Brown_Trucker" title="Twisted Brown Trucker">Twisted Brown Trucker</a> Band, and <a href="/wiki/Devo" title="Devo">Devo</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg/220px-The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg/330px-The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg/440px-The_Cleveland_Orchestra_with_Franz_Welser-M%C3%B6st.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Orchestra" title="Cleveland Orchestra">Cleveland Orchestra</a> (pictured performing at the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Regio_(Turin)" title="Teatro Regio (Turin)">Teatro Regio</a>) is one of the historic <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(orchestras)" title="Big Five (orchestras)">Big Five orchestras</a> in the U.S.</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Playhouse_Square" title="Playhouse Square">Playhouse Square</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> is the nation's second-largest performing arts center, home to ten theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Orchestra" title="Cleveland Orchestra">Cleveland Orchestra</a> is one of the historic <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(orchestras)" title="Big Five (orchestras)">Big Five orchestras</a> in the U.S. and considered among the best worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many other Ohio cities are home to their own orchestras, including <a href="/wiki/Akron_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Akron Symphony Orchestra">Akron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ash_Montgomery_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Blue Ash Montgomery Symphony Orchestra">Blue Ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Canton Symphony Orchestra">Canton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Cincinnati Symphony Orchestra">Cincinnati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Columbus Symphony Orchestra">Columbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Dayton Philharmonic Orchestra">Dayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Toledo Symphony Orchestra">Toledo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Youngstown_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Youngstown Symphony Orchestra">Youngstown</a>. Cincinnati is home to its own <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Ballet" title="Cincinnati Ballet">ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Cincinnati Symphony Orchestra">symphony orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Pops_Orchestra" title="Cincinnati Pops Orchestra">pops orchestra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Opera" title="Cincinnati Opera">opera</a>, all housed at the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Music_Hall" title="Cincinnati Music Hall">Cincinnati Music Hall</a>. Dayton is also home to a ballet, orchestra, and opera, collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Performing_Arts_Alliance" title="Dayton Performing Arts Alliance">Dayton Performing Arts Alliance</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Association_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Columbus Association for the Performing Arts">Columbus Association for the Performing Arts</a> manages seven historic Columbus area theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-bfoc_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfoc-266">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within the marching arts, <a href="/wiki/Winter_Guard_International" title="Winter Guard International">Winter Guard International</a> has hosted national championships in performing arts at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dayton" title="University of Dayton">University of Dayton</a> 18 times between 1983 and 2003, and has permanently since 2005. The <a href="/wiki/Bluecoats_Drum_and_Bugle_Corps" title="Bluecoats Drum and Bugle Corps">Bluecoats Drum and Bugle Corps</a> are Ohio's highest fielding <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bugle_corps_(modern)" title="Drum and bugle corps (modern)">drum corps</a>, competing in the <a href="/wiki/Drum_Corps_International" title="Drum Corps International">Drum Corps International</a> World Class circuit out of <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">Canton</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg/220px-Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg/330px-Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg/440px-Cleveland_Museum_of_Art.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6048" data-file-height="4024" /></a><figcaption>With about 770,000 annual visitors, the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art" title="Cleveland Museum of Art">Cleveland Museum of Art</a> is among the most visited art museums in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-RecordAttendence_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RecordAttendence-267">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio is home to 30 art institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Museum_of_Art" title="Columbus Museum of Art">Columbus Museum of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Art_Museum" title="Cincinnati Art Museum">Cincinnati Art Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art" title="Cleveland Museum of Art">Cleveland Museum of Art</a>, and other entities. The full list includes:
</p>
