</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Art_Museum" title="Cincinnati Art Museum">Cincinnati Art Museum</a> holds over 100,000 works spanning 6,000 years of human history, being among the most comprehensive collections in the <a href="/wiki/Midwest" class="mw-redirect" title="Midwest">Midwest</a>. Among its notable collections are works by Master of San Baudelio, Jorge Ingles, <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">Sandro Botticelli</a> (<i>Judith with Head of Holofernes</i>), <a href="/wiki/Matteo_di_Giovanni" title="Matteo di Giovanni">Matteo di Giovanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Tintoretto" title="Domenico Tintoretto">Domenico Tintoretto</a> (<i>Portrait of Venetian dux Marino Grimani</i>), <a href="/wiki/Mattia_Preti" title="Mattia Preti">Mattia Preti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Strozzi" title="Bernardo Strozzi">Bernardo Strozzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frans_Hals" title="Frans Hals">Frans Hals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Esteban_Murillo" title="Bartolomé Esteban Murillo">Bartolomé Esteban Murillo</a> (<i>St. Thomas of Villanueva</i>), <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Peter Paul Rubens</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Samson_and_Delilah_(Rubens)" title="Samson and Delilah (Rubens)">Samson and Delilah</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Aert_van_der_Neer" title="Aert van der Neer">Aert van der Neer</a>. The collection also includes works by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste-Camille_Corot" title="Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot">Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Auguste_Renoir" title="Pierre-Auguste Renoir">Pierre-Auguste Renoir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camille_Pissarro" title="Camille Pissarro">Camille Pissarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Claude Monet</a> (<i>Rocks At Belle Isle</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a>. The museum also has a large collection of paintings by American painter <a href="/wiki/Frank_Duveneck" title="Frank Duveneck">Frank Duveneck</a> (<i>Elizabeth B. Duveneck</i>).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art" title="Cleveland Museum of Art">Cleveland Museum of Art</a> is internationally renowned for its substantial holdings of <a href="/wiki/Asian_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian art">Asian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_of_ancient_Egypt" title="Art of ancient Egypt">Egyptian</a> art, and has a permanent collection of more than 61,000 works from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-cmageneralinformation_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmageneralinformation-268">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> It is the fourth-wealthiest art museum in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newdirector2014_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newdirector2014-269">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Museum_of_Art" title="Columbus Museum of Art">Columbus Museum of Art</a> holds nineteenth and early twentieth-century American and European art, including early <a href="/wiki/Cubist" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubist">Cubist</a> paintings by <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gris" title="Juan Gris">Juan Gris</a>, works by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boucher" title="François Boucher">François Boucher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_C%C3%A9zanne" title="Paul Cézanne">Paul Cézanne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Cassatt" title="Mary Cassatt">Mary Cassatt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres">Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Degas" title="Edgar Degas">Edgar Degas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse">Henri Matisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Claude Monet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hopper" title="Edward Hopper">Edward Hopper</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norman_Rockwell" title="Norman Rockwell">Norman Rockwell</a>, and installations by <a href="/wiki/Mel_Chin" title="Mel Chin">Mel Chin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josiah_McElheny" title="Josiah McElheny">Josiah McElheny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Philipsz" title="Susan Philipsz">Susan Philipsz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Allan_Sekula" title="Allan Sekula">Allan Sekula</a>. Also in Columbus, the <a href="/wiki/Billy_Ireland_Cartoon_Library_%26_Museum" title="Billy Ireland Cartoon Library &amp; Museum">Billy Ireland Cartoon Library &amp; Museum</a> collection includes 450,000 original cartoons, 36,000 books, 51,000 serial titles, and 3,000 feet (910&#160;m) of manuscript materials, plus 2.5&#160;million comic strip clippings and tear sheets, making it the largest research library for cartoon art.
</p><p>Youngstown's <a href="/wiki/Butler_Institute_of_American_Art" title="Butler Institute of American Art">Butler Institute of American Art</a> was the first museum dedicated exclusively to <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual arts of the United States">American art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vindy-yo-12-29-27_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vindy-yo-12-29-27-270">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Ohio" title="Sports in Ohio">Sports in Ohio</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Professional_sports_teams">Professional sports teams</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:10Cincinnati_2015_(2).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg/220px-10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg/330px-10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg/440px-10Cincinnati_2015_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Great_American_Ball_Park" title="Great American Ball Park">Great American Ball Park</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> baseball team.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio is home to eight professional sports teams across the five different <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major leagues</a> in the United States. Current teams include the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Guardians" title="Cleveland Guardians">Cleveland Guardians</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Crew_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Columbus Crew SC">Columbus Crew SC</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Cincinnati" title="FC Cincinnati">FC Cincinnati</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers" title="Cleveland Cavaliers">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NFL_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFL-275">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Blue_Jackets" title="Columbus Blue Jackets">Columbus Blue Jackets</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ohio has brought home seven <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> titles (Reds 1919, 1940, 1975, 1976, 1990; Indians 1920, 1948), three <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup" title="MLS Cup">MLS Cups</a> (Crew <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2008" title="MLS Cup 2008">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2020" title="MLS Cup 2020">2020</a>, <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2023" title="MLS Cup 2023">2023</a>), one <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Championship</a> (Cavaliers 2016), and nine <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_National_Football_League_championship" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the National Football League championship">NFL Championships</a> (<a href="/wiki/1920_Akron_Pros_season" title="1920 Akron Pros season">Pros 1920</a>; <a href="/wiki/1922_Canton_Bulldogs_season" title="1922 Canton Bulldogs season">Bulldogs 1922</a>, <a href="/wiki/1923_Canton_Bulldogs_season" title="1923 Canton Bulldogs season">1923</a>, <a href="/wiki/1924_Cleveland_Bulldogs_season" title="1924 Cleveland Bulldogs season">1924</a>; <a href="/wiki/1945_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1945 NFL Championship Game">Rams 1945</a>; Browns <a href="/wiki/1950_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1950 NFL Championship Game">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1954 NFL Championship Game">1954</a>, <a href="/wiki/1955_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1955 NFL Championship Game">1955</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1964 NFL Championship Game">1964</a>). Despite this success in the <a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a> in the first half of the 20th century, no Ohio team has won the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> since its inception in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_I" title="Super Bowl I">1967</a>. No Ohio team has made an appearance in the <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="Stanley Cup Finals">Stanley Cup Finals</a>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_(23945852607).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg/220px-Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg/330px-Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg/440px-Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame_%2823945852607%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4011" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> in Canton</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio played a central role in the development of both Major League Baseball and the National Football League. Baseball's first fully professional team, the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Red_Stockings" title="Cincinnati Red Stockings">Cincinnati Red Stockings</a> of 1869, were organized in Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> An informal early-20th-century American football association, the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_League" title="Ohio League">Ohio League</a>, was the direct predecessor of the modern NFL, although neither of Ohio's modern NFL franchises trace their roots to an Ohio League club. The NFL itself was founded in <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">Canton</a> in 1920 as the American Professional Football Conference.<sup id="cite_ref-profootballhof.com_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profootballhof.com-78">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The first official game occurred on October 3, 1920, when the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Triangles" title="Dayton Triangles">Dayton Triangles</a> beat the <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Panhandles" title="Columbus Panhandles">Columbus Panhandles</a> 14–0 in Dayton.<sup id="cite_ref-daytonlocal.com_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daytonlocal.com-79">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Canton was enshrined as the home of the <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-Akron-Canton_Football_Heritage_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Akron-Canton_Football_Heritage-80">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On a smaller scale, Ohio hosts <a href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor league baseball">minor league baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arena_football" title="Arena football">arena football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indoor_American_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Indoor American football">indoor football</a>, mid-level hockey, and lower division soccer.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Individual_sports">Individual sports</h4></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mid-Ohio_Sports_Car_Course" title="Mid-Ohio Sports Car Course">Mid-Ohio Sports Car Course</a> has hosted several auto racing championships, including <a href="/wiki/CART_World_Series" title="CART World Series">CART World Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a>, NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Nationwide_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationwide Series">Nationwide Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Can-Am" title="Can-Am">Can-Am</a>, <a href="/wiki/Formula_5000" title="Formula 5000">Formula 5000</a>, <a href="/wiki/IMSA_GT_Championship" title="IMSA GT Championship">IMSA GT Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rolex_Sports_Car_Series" title="Rolex Sports Car Series">Rolex Sports Car Series</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_of_Cleveland" title="Grand Prix of Cleveland">Grand Prix of Cleveland</a> also hosted CART races from 1982 to 2007. The <a href="/wiki/Eldora_Speedway" title="Eldora Speedway">Eldora Speedway</a> is a major dirt oval that hosts NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Camping_World_Truck_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Camping World Truck Series">Camping World Truck Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_of_Outlaws" title="World of Outlaws">World of Outlaws</a> Sprint Cars and <a href="/wiki/USAC_Silver_Crown_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="USAC Silver Crown Series">USAC Silver Crown Series</a> races.
</p><p>Ohio hosts two <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a> events, the <a href="/wiki/WGC-Bridgestone_Invitational" class="mw-redirect" title="WGC-Bridgestone Invitational">WGC-Bridgestone Invitational</a> and <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Tournament" title="Memorial Tournament">Memorial Tournament</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Masters" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati Masters">Cincinnati Masters</a> is an <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_Masters_1000" class="mw-redirect" title="ATP World Tour Masters 1000">ATP World Tour Masters 1000</a> and <a href="/wiki/WTA_Premier_tournaments" title="WTA Premier tournaments">WTA Premier 5</a> tennis tournament.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="College_sports">College sports</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_Ohio" title="List of college athletic programs in Ohio">List of college athletic programs in Ohio</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Stadium,_Columbus.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg/220px-Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg/330px-Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg/440px-Ohio_Stadium%2C_Columbus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="1332" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Ohio_Stadium" title="Ohio Stadium">Ohio Stadium</a> in Columbus, home to the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football" title="Ohio State Buckeyes football">Ohio State Buckeyes football</a> team, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_stadiums_by_capacity" title="List of stadiums by capacity">fifth-largest stadium</a> in the world.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ohio has eight <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision</a> college football teams, divided among three different <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_conferences" title="List of NCAA conferences">conferences</a>. It has also experienced considerable success in the secondary and tertiary tiers of college football divisions.
</p><p>There are two programs in the <a href="/wiki/Power_Five_conferences" title="Power Five conferences">Power Five conferences</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes" title="Ohio State Buckeyes">Ohio State Buckeyes</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bearcats" title="Cincinnati Bearcats">Cincinnati Bearcats</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football" title="Ohio State Buckeyes football">Ohio State Buckeyes football</a> team is second in all-time winning percentage, with a 931–327–53 overall record and a 25–26 <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowl record</a> as of <a href="/wiki/2020_Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football_team" title="2020 Ohio State Buckeyes football team">2020</a>. The program has produced seven <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> winners, forty conference titles, and eight undisputed national championships. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_men%27s_basketball" title="Ohio State Buckeyes men&#39;s basketball">men's basketball</a> program has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_tournament" title="NCAA Division I men&#39;s basketball tournament">NCAA Division I men's basketball tournament</a> 27 times.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bearcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Cincinnati Bearcats men&#39;s basketball">Cincinnati Bearcats men's basketball</a> team has over 1,800 wins and 33 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_tournament" title="NCAA Division I men&#39;s basketball tournament">March Madness</a> appearances, whilst the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bearcats_football" title="Cincinnati Bearcats football">Bearcats football</a> team became the first <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Five_conferences" title="Group of Five conferences">so-called "Group of Five"</a> team to qualify to the <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Playoff" title="College Football Playoff">College Football Playoff</a> in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Group of Five conferences, six teams are represented in the <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">Mid-American Conference</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Akron_Zips" title="Akron Zips">Akron Zips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green_Falcons" title="Bowling Green Falcons">Bowling Green Falcons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_Golden_Flashes" title="Kent State Golden Flashes">Kent State Golden Flashes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_RedHawks" title="Miami RedHawks">Miami RedHawks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Bobcats" title="Ohio Bobcats">Ohio Bobcats</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Rockets" title="Toledo Rockets">Toledo Rockets</a>. The MAC headquarters are in Cleveland. The <a href="/wiki/Victory_Bell_(Cincinnati%E2%80%93Miami)" title="Victory Bell (Cincinnati–Miami)">Cincinnati–Miami</a> rivalry game has been played in southwest Ohio every year since 1888 and is the oldest current non-conference <a href="/wiki/NCAA_football" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA football">NCAA football</a> rivalry.
</p><p>Other Division I schools, either part of the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship Subdivision">NCAA Division I Football Championship Subdivision</a> or not fielding in football include the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_State_Vikings" title="Cleveland State Vikings">Cleveland State Vikings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Musketeers" title="Xavier Musketeers">Xavier Musketeers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wright_State_Raiders" title="Wright State Raiders">Wright State Raiders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Youngstown_State_Penguins" title="Youngstown State Penguins">Youngstown State Penguins</a>. Xavier's <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Musketeers_men%27s_basketball" title="Xavier Musketeers men&#39;s basketball">men's basketball</a> has performed particularly well, with 27 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_tournament" title="NCAA Division I men&#39;s basketball tournament">March Madness</a> appearances. Youngstown State's <a href="/wiki/Youngstown_State_Penguins_football" title="Youngstown State Penguins football">football</a> has the third most <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">NCAA Division I Football Championship</a> wins, with 3.
</p><p>There are 12 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">NCAA Division II</a> universities and 22 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">NCAA Division III</a> universities in Ohio.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1217336898">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the U.S. Census<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>, Greater Columbus is the largest <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">Metropolitan statistical area</a> (MSA) that is <i>entirely within</i> Ohio, with a population of 2,078,725; and Greater Cincinnati is the largest MSA that is <i>at least partially</i> within Ohio, with a population of 2,179,082, approximately 25% of which is in Indiana or Kentucky. Which MSA is the largest <i>in Ohio</i> depends on the context.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-NAVD88-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NAVD88_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NAVD88_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Elevation adjusted to <a href="/wiki/North_American_Vertical_Datum_of_1988" title="North American Vertical Datum of 1988">North American Vertical Datum of 1988</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Petun" title="Petun">Petun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erie_people" title="Erie people">Erie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutral Nation">Chonnonton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">Wyandot</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mingo" title="Mingo">Mingo Seneca</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Iroquois Confederacy</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Miami_people" title="Miami people">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mascouten" title="Mascouten">Mascouten</a> <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Lenape</a> <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odawa" title="Odawa">Odawa</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Mosopelea" title="Mosopelea">Mosopelea</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The last French Fort in Ohio Country, Fort Sandusky, was destroyed in 1763 during Pontiac's Rebellion.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Persons of Hispanic or Latino origin are not distinguished between total and partial ancestry.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
